    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app',

<span id="freeTextContainer17092750432881295085">Nach einer Blinddarmoperation ist Kims kleine Schwester nicht mehr aus der Narkose aufgewacht, sie liegt im Koma.   <span id="freeText17092750432881295085" style="display:none">Nach einer Blinddarmoperation ist Kims kleine Schwester nicht mehr aus der Narkose aufgewacht, sie liegt im Koma. Die Stimmung in der Familie ist gedrückt, als Kim an diesem Abend ins Bett geht. Da sieht er in einer Ecke seines Zimmers plötzlich einen alten Mann.<br /><br />Der Alte erklärt Kim, seine Schwester werde im Land Märchenmond vom bösen Boraas gefangengehalten. Mit einem Raumgleiter aus einem SF-Roman macht sich Kim sofort auf, um seine Schwester zu retten. Doch er hat Pech und landet mitten im Reich von Boraas, auf der besetzten Seite des friedlichen Märchenlandes. Unter großen Gefahren gelingt es Kim, vor Boraas zu fliehen, und in der Verkleidung eines feindlichen schwarzen Ritters gelangt er mit Boraas Armeee über das Schneegebirge nach Märchenmond.<br /><br />Dort erfährt er, daß er zunächst den König des Regenbogens suchen muß, der noch weit hinter dem Ende der Welt lebt. Zusammen mit seinen neuen Freunden macht sich Kim auf seinen abenteuerlichen Weg.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1650420114814182837">This book is a like a combination of Lord of the Rings and Narnia but then super boring and dull to read.<br/>From the first page till the last, the story didn't grab me at all. The characters are annoying and not original, they all are a cliche of well known character treats. The story is slow throughout the whole book and only in the last few chapter there finally is something happening but even that is boring. It all feels like those super cliche happy ending dramatic movies with a cliche message </span>
  <span id="freeText1650420114814182837" style="display:none">This book is a like a combination of Lord of the Rings and Narnia but then super boring and dull to read.<br />From the first page till the last, the story didn't grab me at all. The characters are annoying and not original, they all are a cliche of well known character treats. The story is slow throughout the whole book and only in the last few chapter there finally is something happening but even that is boring. It all feels like those super cliche happy ending dramatic movies with a cliche message in every chapter. I will never ever read this book again or read the second book because this book took way to much time which I could have been spending on a better book then this one.</span>

<div id="review_1074678036" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1074678036" />
    <a title="Emerson  Chan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12781764-emerson-chan"><img alt="Emerson  Chan" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1074678036?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emerson  Chan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emerson  Chan" href="/user/show/12781764-emerson-chan">Emerson  Chan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1074678036" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14483813064405890754">As a young boy, I was always naive about good and bad. However, my sister changed my mind. My sister recommended me this book called <u> Magic Moon </u>. It was an english verison of a german book. <br/><br/>Summary<br/>The main character was a boy named Kim. His sister had recently went into comma. As he worried about her, she appeared in his dreams. He had to go on a journey to find the secrets that kept his sister asleep. He fights fantastical creatures and the dark lord, whom tried to rule everyone in the land. E</span>
  <span id="freeText14483813064405890754" style="display:none">As a young boy, I was always naive about good and bad. However, my sister changed my mind. My sister recommended me this book called <u> Magic Moon </u>. It was an english verison of a german book. <br /><br />Summary<br />The main character was a boy named Kim. His sister had recently went into comma. As he worried about her, she appeared in his dreams. He had to go on a journey to find the secrets that kept his sister asleep. He fights fantastical creatures and the dark lord, whom tried to rule everyone in the land. Even though, the main conflict was his sister's well-being, the conflict between him and the dark lord was the event that captivated me. It showed that everyone has balance within them. In page 331 it reads, "Kim cried out in horror when he saw the Black Lord's face. It was his own! The Black Lord was none other than himself!" In addition, on page 332 it says,"The Black Lord was his mirror image, the essence of all his bad characteristics, the incaration of all the selfish thoughts he'd in his life." Another quote is, "'Every person has good and evil in him. One cannot exist without the other.'" This shows how everyone has a split personality. They are good and evil at the same time. In this world, not everyone is automatically good or bad. They have bad and good characteristics. It is all about how they want to fix or change them. This book taught me to be open-minded and look at other people in a different way.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14483813064405890754" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1822993335" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15683964607136255386">Als Jugendbuch für 10-12-Jährige mag es durchgehen, insgesamt ist die Story aber recht flach (wirkt für mich wie ein Abklatsch der Unendlichen Geschichte (Michael Ende)) und ist recht vorausschaubar.<br/><br/>Gleichzeitig enthält sie diverse unlogische Elemente. Es ist bei Jugendbüchern nicht ungewöhnlich, dass die Protagonisten, sobald sie mal ein Schwert finden, sofort zum Meisterkämpfer mutieren (ohne jegliches Training), doch warum Kim relativ zu Beginn (natürlich mit Hilfe) ohne jegliche Gewissensbis</span>
  <span id="freeText15683964607136255386" style="display:none">Als Jugendbuch für 10-12-Jährige mag es durchgehen, insgesamt ist die Story aber recht flach (wirkt für mich wie ein Abklatsch der Unendlichen Geschichte (Michael Ende)) und ist recht vorausschaubar.<br /><br />Gleichzeitig enthält sie diverse unlogische Elemente. Es ist bei Jugendbüchern nicht ungewöhnlich, dass die Protagonisten, sobald sie mal ein Schwert finden, sofort zum Meisterkämpfer mutieren (ohne jegliches Training), doch warum Kim relativ zu Beginn (natürlich mit Hilfe) ohne jegliche Gewissensbisse gegen 10-20 Gegner kämpft (und natürlich gewinnt), am Schluss aber plötzlich fast verzweifelt, weil sich sein Erzfeind mehr oder weniger selber auf dem Schwert aufgespießt hat, muss man nicht verstehen.<br /><br />Auch habe ich als Fantasyfan prinzipiell nichts gegen waffenlos kämpfende Charaktere, aber warum man ausgerechnet Steppenreiter dafür vorsehen muss und vor allem, wie man auf einem Pferderücken sinnvoll ohne Waffen gegen andere gepanzerte und bewaffnete Reiter kämpft, will sich mir beim besten Willen nicht erschließen.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15683964607136255386" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2496690547" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2496690547" />
    <a title="Alger Smythe-Hopkins" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16757678-alger-smythe-hopkins"><img alt="Alger Smythe-Hopkins" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1359036794p2/16757678.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2496690547?book_show_action=true">Aug 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alger Smythe-Hopkins" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alger Smythe-Hopkins" href="/user/show/16757678-alger-smythe-hopkins">Alger Smythe-Hopkins</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781598164527" href="/book/show/97161.Magic_Moon">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2496690547" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14785945610675829935">The plot of this book rhymes with a young adult fantasy (hence all the references to <i>Narnia</i>), but it isn't anything like a coherent novel. Perhaps some of the problem lies in translation, if the title is any guide (Märchenmond means something closer to Fableland) the translator took considerable liberties. But translation can only go so far towards explaining why this charmless book feels like an story made up as it went along. There are innumerable places where the description simply makes no s</span>
  <span id="freeText14785945610675829935" style="display:none">The plot of this book rhymes with a young adult fantasy (hence all the references to <i>Narnia</i>), but it isn't anything like a coherent novel. Perhaps some of the problem lies in translation, if the title is any guide (Märchenmond means something closer to Fableland) the translator took considerable liberties. But translation can only go so far towards explaining why this charmless book feels like an story made up as it went along. There are innumerable places where the description simply makes no sense to the action, and most of what happens seems only to be included because the author thought t should be included in a fantasy novel. One of the strangest inventions is a formidable army of martial arts cavalry, which really just makes no sense if you stop to think about it. How do you perform hand to hand combat from the back of a horse? There is also a bizarre unstability to how the book values lives. At some points the boy-hero happily slashes his way through an army of the enemy, but long after this he suddenly has a revulsion at the thought of murder and vows never to kill again. Then in the next fight he goes right back to hacking and slashing. The ending is a cliched 'we are all our own worst enemy' bit of nonsense that borrows simultaneously from the <i>Wizard of Oz</i> and <i>The Strange Case of Dr. Jekyll and Mr Hyde</i> but without giving a sense of closure. A book marked by strange aimless rambling with a kind of dream-logic formulation, and random unsatisfactory situations.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14785945610675829935" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3633066349" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12607224566653912984">Das Buch ist ein gutes Beispiel für die Trope des Auserwählten, der hier in der Form eines 23jährigen daherkommt, der ausgewachsene Krieger besiegt. Eine Quest, eine Reise, Gut und Böse, blabla. An der Formelhaftigkeit der Geschichte kann auch das übrrstürzte Moralkeulenende nichts ändern. Stellenweise ist die Story ganz unterhaltsam und als sie rauskam, war sie bestimmt auch noch nicht so oft erzählt worden. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2394189370754628872">Dieses Buch ist eine sehr ansprechende Kinderserie. Durch die Kombination aus real und fantastisch entsteht ein besonderes Lese-ereignis. Denn, aus diesen besteht das ganze Land Märchenmond.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1695385149" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1695385149" />
    <a title="Aelvana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33911745-aelvana"><img alt="Aelvana" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1695385149?book_show_action=true">Jul 11, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aelvana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aelvana" href="/user/show/33911745-aelvana">Aelvana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781598164527" href="/book/show/97161.Magic_Moon">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1695385149" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14486368659889387910">Kim prefers science fiction to real life, but even he can't imagine the real cause of his little sister's inexplicable coma. When he's invited to the world of Magic Moon, where his sister used to play until her illness, he has a chance to save her---and that world. But Boreas and the Realm of Shadows want him, too. He sees Kim as his opportunity to finally bring all of Magic Moon under the reign of evil . . .<br/><br/>This was an unexpected surprise. The alternate world of Magic Moon isn't always sketched</span>
  <span id="freeText14486368659889387910" style="display:none">Kim prefers science fiction to real life, but even he can't imagine the real cause of his little sister's inexplicable coma. When he's invited to the world of Magic Moon, where his sister used to play until her illness, he has a chance to save her---and that world. But Boreas and the Realm of Shadows want him, too. He sees Kim as his opportunity to finally bring all of Magic Moon under the reign of evil . . .<br /><br />This was an unexpected surprise. The alternate world of Magic Moon isn't always sketched out fully, but what we do see is a world that feels born of myth and magic. I liked the characters, especially some of the side characters like Tak (all the Taks, haha), Kelhim, and Rangarig. Dragons that can knock buildings down if they laugh too hard amuse me. And the Rainbow King. My favorite line from him: "Another one of your human superstitions. I am immortal. Why should I run around looking like a frail old man when I can choose any age I please?"<br /><br />Although I disagree heartily with much of the philosophy, I did like the twist near the end (though, not the one that rendered everyone's deaths pointless, as that was a little too much cheating). The Black Lord and his connection to Boreas was nicely played, and how Kim ends up fighting them was the last thing I expected. <br /><br />I did think Magic Moon's attitude towards death in general misses the point. Yes, it happens to everyone, but acting as though the mere memory of the person is just as good as having the person with you ignores the fact that death is the final separation. That's why people grieve: the only thing that remains for the living are memories. So it was an interesting speculation, but ultimately one I found too hard to swallow. <br /><br />All in all this is an interesting little book, but given that it was published by Tokyopop (who went out of business several years ago) and has a cover that doesn't hint very well what type of story it is, I don't imagine too many people are going to find it these days. I rate this book Recommended.<br /><br />See my reviews and more at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://offtheshelfreviews.wordpress.com/">https://offtheshelfreviews.wordpress....</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="14486368659889387910" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_119108953" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/119108953" />
    <a title="Hikari" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4218407-hikari"><img alt="Hikari" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1283073425p2/4218407.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/119108953?book_show_action=true">Aug 29, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hikari" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hikari" href="/user/show/4218407-hikari">Hikari</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer119108953" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14955040065399670125">Märchenmond von den Holhbeins ist ein wirklich wunderschönes Fantasybuch.<br/><br/>Der Junge Kim liest für sein Leben gern Sci-Fi-Bücher und wäre auch gern ein solcher Sternenkrieger oder Pilot.<br/>Seine kleine Schwester Rebekka liegt auf der Intensivstation eines Krankenhauses und die Ärzte sind ratlos, was mit der Kleinen passiert ist.<br/><br/>Während eines Besuches bei ihr sieht Kim einen alten Mann, der ihn auch später beim Besuch in einem Café betrachtet. Des Nachts taucht der alte Mann bei ihm auf und kündigt ih</span>
  <span id="freeText14955040065399670125" style="display:none">Märchenmond von den Holhbeins ist ein wirklich wunderschönes Fantasybuch.<br /><br />Der Junge Kim liest für sein Leben gern Sci-Fi-Bücher und wäre auch gern ein solcher Sternenkrieger oder Pilot.<br />Seine kleine Schwester Rebekka liegt auf der Intensivstation eines Krankenhauses und die Ärzte sind ratlos, was mit der Kleinen passiert ist.<br /><br />Während eines Besuches bei ihr sieht Kim einen alten Mann, der ihn auch später beim Besuch in einem Café betrachtet. Des Nachts taucht der alte Mann bei ihm auf und kündigt ihm an, dass er seine Hilfe braucht, da nämlich nur Kim helfen kann. Und zwar soll er Rebekka retten, seine eigene Schwester! Das kleine Mädchen wurde bei ihrem Besuch in Märchenmond, das Land, aus dem der alte Mann kommt, von dem bösen und finsteren Herrscher Booras gefangen genommen, der finstere Pläne ausheckt und dessen Ziel es ist, ganz Märchenmond zu vernichten.<br /><br />Kim beschließt sofort, Märchenmond und seine Schwester zu retten. Doch gibt es für jeden Menschen einen eigenen Zugang, so auch für Kim, den er ganz alleine finden muss. Der Junge findet schließlich seinen eigenen Weg und gelangt mit Müh und Not nach einigen Abenteuern nach Märchenmond.<br /><br />Hier findet er Freunde, trifft aber auch auf viele Gefahren und Feinde. Und schließlich muss er dem bösen Herrscher selbst gegenübertreten.<br /><br /><br />Mit dem Stil von Märchenmond bin ich größtenteils zufrieden, doch gibt es ein paar kleinere Schwächen dabei, die sich aber in einem der folgenden Bände, "Märchenmonds Kinder", geben.<br /><br />Doch trotzdem ist Märchenmond ein fantastisches Abenteuer, dass jeder einmal bestritten haben sollte. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14955040065399670125" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_21685843" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/21685843" />
    <a title="Jennifer Wardrip" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1125613-jennifer-wardrip"><img alt="Jennifer Wardrip" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442657515p2/1125613.jpg" /></a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781598164527" href="/book/show/97161.Magic_Moon">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1125613-jennifer-wardrip?shelf=trt-posted-reviews">trt-posted-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1125613-jennifer-wardrip?shelf=read-by-other-reviewers">read-by-other-reviewers</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer21685843" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9052018410951010103">Reviewed by Carrie Spellman for TeensReadToo.com<br/><br/>Kim is a pretty normal kid--he has a normal family, and a normal life. He's even a pretty normal student, who would rather read his favorite new fantasy/adventure series than do his math homework. Until his four-year-old sister goes to the hospital for a standard operation, and doesn't wake up afterwards. Now she's in a coma, and Kim, his parents, and even the doctors don't know what to do. Except that maybe there is something Kim can do. <br/><br/>After bei</span>
  <span id="freeText9052018410951010103" style="display:none">Reviewed by Carrie Spellman for TeensReadToo.com<br /><br />Kim is a pretty normal kid--he has a normal family, and a normal life. He's even a pretty normal student, who would rather read his favorite new fantasy/adventure series than do his math homework. Until his four-year-old sister goes to the hospital for a standard operation, and doesn't wake up afterwards. Now she's in a coma, and Kim, his parents, and even the doctors don't know what to do. Except that maybe there is something Kim can do. <br /><br />After being at the hospital one night, Kim is visited by a man. The man says Kim's sister named him Themistokles, and it stuck. Themistokles is from Magic Moon, also named by his sister, and an evil man is holding her captive. Kim has to come to Magic Moon and save her, but he also has to find his own way there. How do you find a way to a magical place that you've never heard of before? Kim tries to follow Themistokles and finds a rocket ship/fighter jet parked in front of his house. Amazingly, Kim can fly it. It takes him right to Magic Moon. Well, almost. He crashes in the Shadowland. Now, Kim has to save himself, and possibly all of Magic Moon. <br /><br />Part LORD OF THE RINGS, part CHRONICLES OF NARNIA, with a little eastern philosophy thrown in, this is a great adventure in an amazingly well-imagined world. It's definitely an involved story that might seem like a bit too much to handle, but it's nothing to fans of THE HOBBIT and LORD OF THE RINGS. </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer875807017181503772">Wolfgand and Heike hohlbein have wriiten fantasy in which you are taken just a step away rom our normal world and enter dangerous territory</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16424522104419072966">This is a book by a German author who has largely been undiscoveerd in the English language, which is a great pity. A boy must venture into a magic land that his sister had discovered to save her there so that she might be saved from her life threatening illness in the real world.<br/><br/>The world of Magic Moon is beautifully drawn, and strongly put me in mind of the Neverending Story (also by a</span>
  <span id="freeText16424522104419072966" style="display:none">This is a book by a German author who has largely been undiscoveerd in the English language, which is a great pity. A boy must venture into a magic land that his sister had discovered to save her there so that she might be saved from her life threatening illness in the real world.<br /><br />The world of Magic Moon is beautifully drawn, and strongly put me in mind of the Neverending Story (also by a German author).<br /><br />I enjoyed this book even though it was written for younger readers - and should be enjoyable to children of about 8+.</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('uwR6rOXaQCrN/KGf+RWRVE84T3ZomsLDbE0Zqid/KMOEGxv+vuB0pMppe53WcLKuCGspvQtZL4KashB0nIUaqQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('p13Ju5V71dbH6Vcp8+9dC4pNxqb025DTRg2DTrsDKvCYQqjpzkHhWMB8jSvcin7xzR6gbZcYfZKw8oqQAPkYmg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/40343.Wolfgang_Hohlbein">About Wolfgang Hohlbein</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/40343.Wolfgang_Hohlbein"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1207241532p3/40343.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/40343.Wolfgang_Hohlbein">Wolfgang Hohlbein
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
347
followers
</div>

</div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer862599221673717632">Wolfgang Hohlbein is a German author of science fiction, fantasy and horror fiction who lives near Neuss, North Rhine-Westphalia. His wife, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/40342.Heike' title='Heike' rel='nofollow noopener'>Heike</a>, is also a writer and often works with her husband. She often comes up with the story ideas and therefore is generally credited as co-author. Their daughter, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/436369.Rebecca' title='Rebecca' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rebecca</a>, is also a writer.<br/> <br/>Writing short stories since age 15, Hohlbein was first recognized as </span>
  <span id="freeText862599221673717632" style="display:none">Wolfgang Hohlbein is a German author of science fiction, fantasy and horror fiction who lives near Neuss, North Rhine-Westphalia. His wife, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/40342.Heike" title="Heike" rel="nofollow noopener">Heike</a>, is also a writer and often works with her husband. She often comes up with the story ideas and therefore is generally credited as co-author. Their daughter, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/436369.Rebecca" title="Rebecca" rel="nofollow noopener">Rebecca</a>, is also a writer.<br /> <br />Writing short stories since age 15, Hohlbein was first recognized as an author after sending in a manuscript he and his wife had written at a fantasy and science fiction writing contest in 1982. They won and their book, <i>Märchenmond</i> (English title: "Magic Moon"), was published by Ueberreuter Publishing, soon becoming a bestseller and winning several awards. It is one of their greatest successes till today.<br /> <br />Many of his more than 200 books are translated and published in many European countries as well as in South Korea. Yet for many years none of his works had been translated into English. In 2006, <i>Magic Moon</i> was translated into English and published in the United States.</span>
  <a data-text-id="862599221673717632" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
